<li id="cite_note-_260fe24fb4297682-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-_260fe24fb4297682_15-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMasters_of_Doom2003">Masters of Doom, 2003</a>, p. 73: «The id guys arrived at the apartment in Madison on a gray day in September 1991 [..] id team buck- led down to finish the second Commander Keen trilogy».</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-_d5bf6d42a9d6abda-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-_d5bf6d42a9d6abda_16-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMasters_of_Doom2003">Masters of Doom, 2003</a>, pp. 74—75: «“Texture mapping?” Carmack replied, then took a few seconds to spin the concept around in his head. “I can do that.” [..] The result was Catacomb 3-D, which incorporated texture-mapped walls of gray bricks covered in green slime».</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-_52ff279468f17f44-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-_52ff279468f17f44_17-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMasters_of_Doom2003">Masters of Doom, 2003</a>, pp. 75: «When Scott Miller saw Catacomb 3-D, he had one thing to say: “We need to do something like this as shareware.”».</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-_0edbd68b60a2f1c6-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-_0edbd68b60a2f1c6_18-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMasters_of_Doom2003">Masters of Doom, 2003</a>, p. 76: «The trouble started with Tom. Buoyed by the blockbuster success of the first trilogy months before, he had long imagined doing three trilogies [..] But Carmack’s technology was clearly headed toward another idea; a fast-action, first-person game.».</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-_652cb7a2374c0a14-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-_652cb7a2374c0a14_19-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMasters_of_Doom2003">Masters of Doom, 2003</a>, p. 77: «“Yeah, I don’t know,” Romero said. “You know, it’d be really fucking cool if we made a remake of Castle Wolfenstein and did it in 3-D.”».</span>
</li>

In the original Wolfenstein, the characters could search the bodies of dead soldiers».</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-_aa8e7a008db53d6d-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-_aa8e7a008db53d6d_22-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMasters_of_Doom2003">Masters of Doom, 2003</a>, p. 77: «Wolfenstein could be like nothing the industry had ever seen. “It will be just shocking,” Romero concluded, “a totally shocking game.”».</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-_a34b003ae3d0f3f4-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-_a34b003ae3d0f3f4_23-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMasters_of_Doom2003">Masters of Doom, 2003</a>, p. 77: «Carmack was growing to appreciate Romero’s talent for taking his technology into a new world, a place he himself would never have conceived. Adrian, who wasn’t familiar with the original Wolfenstein, was eager to do anything other than Keen, and the idea of 3-D art intrigued him. Tom, though stung by the rejection of Keen, assumed that they would return to his games after this one».</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-_17173d5bd3d54395-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-_17173d5bd3d54395_25-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMasters_of_Doom2003">Masters of Doom, 2003</a>, p. 78: «At first they assumed they had to use something other than the Wolfenstein name, which had been created by Silas Warner at Muse Software».</span>

<li id="cite_note-_971fac43e45bf1fa-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-_971fac43e45bf1fa_30-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMasters_of_Doom2003">Masters of Doom, 2003</a>, p. 79: «Mark Rein, still id’s probationary president, had scored with FormGen to release two more retail id products. <li id="cite_note-_99bdcffe5120fa76-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-_99bdcffe5120fa76_31-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMasters_of_Doom2003">Masters of Doom, 2003</a>, pp. 79—80: «as he said, “to mow down Nazis.” [..] shock and horror of storming a Nazi bunker [..] “lots of blood, blood like you never see in games” [..] Tom came up with treasures and crosses for players to find».</span>
